   28: =head1 NAME
   29: 
   30: App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor - Extract test schemas from Perl modules
   31: 
   32: =head1 VERSION
   33: 
   34: Version 0.32
   35: 
   36: =head1 SYNOPSIS
   37: 
   38: 	use App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor;
   39: 
   40: 	my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
   41: 		input_file => 'lib/MyModule.pm',
   42: 		output_dir => 'schemas/',
   43: 		verbose	=> 1,
   44: 	);
   45: 
   46: 	my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
   47: 
   48: =head1 DESCRIPTION
   49: 
   50: App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor analyzes Perl modules and generates
   51: structured YAML schema files suitable for automated test generation by L<App::Test::Generator>.
   52: This module employs
   53: static analysis techniques to infer parameter types, constraints, and
   54: method behaviors directly from your source code.
   55: 
   56: =head2 Analysis Methods
   57: 
   58: The extractor combines multiple analysis approaches for a comprehensive schema generation:
   59: 
   60: =over 4
   61: 
   62: =item * B<POD Documentation Analysis>
   63: 
   64: Parses embedded documentation to extract:
   65:   - Parameter names, types, and descriptions from =head2 sections
   66:   - Method signatures with positional parameters
   67:   - Return value specifications from "Returns:" sections
   68:   - Constraints (ranges, patterns, required/optional status)
   69:   - Semantic type detection (email, URL, filename)
   70: 
   71: =item * B<Code Pattern Detection>
   72: 
   73: Analyzes source code using PPI to identify:
   74:   - Method signatures and parameter extraction patterns
   75:   - Type validation (ref(), isa(), blessed())
   76:   - Constraint patterns (length checks, numeric comparisons, regex matches)
   77:   - Return statement analysis and value type inference
   78:   - Object instantiation requirements and accessor methods
   79: 
   80: =item * B<Signature Analysis>
   81: 
   82: Examines method declarations for:
   83:   - Parameter names and positional information
   84:   - Instance vs. class method detection
   85:   - Method modifiers (Moose-style before/after/around)
   86:   - Various parameter declaration styles (shift, @_ assignment)
   87: 
   88: =item * B<Heuristic Inference>
   89: 
   90: Applies Perl-specific domain knowledge:
   91:   - Boolean return detection from method names (is_*, has_*, can_*)
   92:   - Common Perl idioms and coding patterns
   93:   - Context awareness (scalar vs list, wantarray usage)
   94:   - Object-oriented patterns (constructors, accessors, chaining)
   95: 
   96: =back
   97: 
   98: =head2 Generated Schema Structure
   99: 
  100: The extracted schemas follow this YAML structure:
  101: 
  102:     function: method_name
  103:     module: Package::Name
  104:     input:
  105:       param1:
  106:         type: string
  107:         min: 3
  108:         max: 50
  109:         optional: 0
  110:         position: 0
  111:       param2:
  112:         type: integer
  113:         min: 0
  114:         max: 100
  115:         optional: 1
  116:         position: 1
  117:     output:
  118:       type: boolean
  119:       value: 1
  120:     new: Package::Name # if object instantiation required
  121:     config:
  122:       test_empty: 1
  123:       test_nuls: 0
  124:       test_undef: 0
  125:       test_non_ascii: 0
  126: 
  127: =head2 Advanced Detection Capabilities
  128: 
  129: =over 4
  130: 
  131: =item * B<Accessor Method Detection>
  132: 
  133: Automatically identifies getter, setter, and combined accessor methods
  134: by analyzing common patterns like C<return $self-E<gt>{property}> and
  135: C<$self-E<gt>{property} = $value>.
  136: 
  137: =item * B<Boolean Return Inference>
  138: 
  139: Detects boolean-returning methods through multiple signals:
  140:   - Method name patterns (is_*, has_*, can_*)
  141:   - Return patterns (consistent 1/0 returns)
  142:   - POD descriptions ("returns true on success")
  143:   - Ternary operators with boolean results
  144: 
  145: =item * B<Context Awareness>
  146: 
  147: Identifies methods that use C<wantarray> and can return different
  148: values in scalar vs list context.
  149: 
  150: =item * B<Object Lifecycle Management>
  151: 
  152: Detects instance methods requiring object instantiation and
  153: automatically adds the C<new> field to schemas.
  154: 
  155: =item * B<Enhanced Object Detection>
  156: 
  157: The extractor includes sophisticated object detection capabilities that go beyond simple instance method identification:
  158: 
  159: =over 4
  160: 
  161: =item * B<Factory Method Recognition>
  162: 
  163: Automatically identifies methods that create and return object instances, such as methods named C<create_*>, C<make_*>, C<build_*>, or C<get_*>. Factory methods are correctly classified as class methods that don't require pre-existing objects for testing.
  164: 
  165: =item * B<Singleton Pattern Detection>
  166: 
  167: Recognizes singleton patterns through multiple signals: method names like C<instance> or C<get_instance>, static variables holding instance references, lazy initialization patterns (C<$instance ||= new()>), and consistent return of the same instance variable.
  168: 
  169: =item * B<Constructor Parameter Analysis>
  170: 
  171: Examines C<new> methods to determine required and optional parameters, validation requirements, and default values. This enables test generators to provide appropriate constructor arguments when object instantiation is needed.
  172: 
  173: =item * B<Inheritance Relationship Handling>
  174: 
  175: Detects parent classes through C<use parent>, C<use base>, and C<@ISA> declarations. Identifies when methods use C<SUPER::> calls and determines whether the current class or a parent class constructor should be used for object instantiation.
  176: 
  177: =item * B<External Object Dependency Detection>
  178: 
  179: Identifies when methods create or depend on objects from other classes, enabling proper test setup with mock objects or real dependencies.
  180: 
  181: =back
  182: 
  183: These enhancements ensure that generated test schemas accurately reflect the object-oriented structure of the code, leading to more meaningful and effective test generation.
  184: 
  185: =back
  186: 
  187: =head2 Confidence Scoring
  188: 
  189: Each generated schema includes detailed confidence assessments:
  190: 
  191: =over 4
  192: 
  193: =item * B<High Confidence>
  194: 
  195: Multiple independent analysis sources converge on consistent,
  196: well-constrained parameters with explicit validation logic and
  197: comprehensive documentation.
  198: 
  199: =item * B<Medium Confidence>
  200: 
  201: Reasonable evidence from code patterns or partial documentation,
  202: but may lack comprehensive constraints or have some ambiguities.
  203: 
  204: =item * B<Low Confidence>
  205: 
  206: Minimal evidence - primarily based on naming conventions,
  207: default assumptions, or single-source analysis.
  208: 
  209: =item * B<Very Low Confidence>
  210: 
  211: Barely any detectable signals - schema should be thoroughly
  212: reviewed before use in test generation.
  213: 
  214: =back
  215: 
  216: =head2 Use Cases
  217: 
  218: =over 4
  219: 
  220: =item * B<Automated Test Generation>
  221: 
  222: Generate comprehensive test suites with L<App::Test::Generator> using
  223: extracted schemas as input. The schemas provide the necessary structure
  224: for generating both positive and negative test cases.
  225: 
  226: =item * B<API Documentation Generation>
  227: 
  228: Supplement existing documentation with automatically inferred interface
  229: specifications, parameter requirements, and return types.
  230: 
  231: =item * B<Code Quality Assessment>
  232: 
  233: Identify methods with poor documentation, inconsistent parameter handling,
  234: or unclear interfaces that may benefit from refactoring.
  235: 
  236: =item * B<Refactoring Assistance>
  237: 
  238: Detect method dependencies, object instantiation requirements, and
  239: parameter usage patterns to inform refactoring decisions.
  240: 
  241: =item * B<Legacy Code Analysis>
  242: 
  243: Quickly understand the interface contracts of legacy Perl codebases
  244: without extensive manual code reading.
  245: 
  246: =back
  247: 
  248: =head2 Integration with Testing Ecosystem
  249: 
  250: The generated schemas are specifically designed to work with the
  251: L<App::Test::Generator> ecosystem:
  252: 
  253:     # Extract schemas from your module
  254:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(...);
  255:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
  256: 
  257:     # Use with test generator (typically as separate steps)
  258:     # fuzz-harness-generator -r schemas/method_name.yml
  259: 
  260: =head2 Limitations and Considerations
  261: 
  262: =over 4
  263: 
  264: =item * B<Dynamic Code Patterns>
  265: 
  266: Highly dynamic code (string evals, AUTOLOAD, symbolic references)
  267: may not be fully detected by static analysis.
  268: 
  269: =item * B<Complex Validation Logic>
  270: 
  271: Sophisticated validation involving multiple parameters or external
  272: dependencies may require manual schema refinement.
  273: 
  274: =item * B<Confidence Heuristics>
  275: 
  276: Confidence scores are based on heuristics and should be reviewed
  277: by developers familiar with the codebase.
  278: 
  279: =item * B<Perl Idiom Recognition>
  280: 
  281: Some Perl-specific idioms may require custom pattern recognition
  282: beyond the built-in detectors.
  283: 
  284: =item * B<Documentation Dependency>
  285: 
  286: Analysis quality improves significantly with comprehensive POD
  287: documentation following consistent patterns.
  288: 
  289: =back
  290: 
  291: =head2 Best Practices for Optimal Results
  292: 
  293: =over 4
  294: 
  295: =item * B<Comprehensive POD Documentation>
  296: 
  297: Write detailed POD with explicit parameter documentation using
  298: consistent patterns like C<$param - type (constraints), description>.
  299: 
  300: =item * B<Consistent Coding Patterns>
  301: 
  302: Use consistent parameter validation patterns and method signatures
  303: throughout your codebase.
  304: 
  305: =item * B<Schema Review Process>
  306: 
  307: Review and refine automatically generated schemas, particularly
  308: those with low confidence scores.
  309: 
  310: =item * B<Descriptive Naming>
  311: 
  312: Use descriptive method and parameter names that clearly indicate
  313: purpose and expected types.
  314: 
  315: =item * B<Progressive Enhancement>
  316: 
  317: Start with automatically generated schemas and progressively
  318: refine them based on test results and code understanding.
  319: 
  320: =back
  321: 
  322: The module is particularly valuable for large codebases where manual schema
  323: creation would be prohibitively time-consuming, and for maintaining test
  324: coverage as code evolves through continuous integration pipelines.
  325: 
  326: =head2 Advanced Type Detection
  327: 
  328: The schema extractor includes enhanced type detection capabilities that identify specialized Perl types beyond basic strings and integers.
  329: L<DateTime> and L<Time::Piece> objects are detected through isa() checks and method call patterns, while date strings (ISO 8601, YYYY-MM-DD) and UNIX timestamps are recognized through regex validation and numeric range checks.
  330: File handles and file paths are identified via I/O operations and file test operators, coderefs are detected through ref() checks and invocation patterns, and enum-like parameters are extracted from validation code including regex patterns (C</^(a|b|c)$/>), hash lookups, grep statements, and if/elsif chains.
  331: These detected types are preserved in the generated YAML schemas with appropriate semantic annotations, enabling test generators to create more accurate and meaningful test cases.
  332: 
  333: =head3 Example Advanced Type Schema
  334: 
  335: For a method like:
  336: 
  337:     sub process_event {
  338:         my ($self, $timestamp, $status, $callback) = @_;
  339:         croak unless $timestamp > 1000000000;
  340:         croak unless $status =~ /^(active|pending|complete)$/;
  341:         croak unless ref($callback) eq 'CODE';
  342:         $callback->($timestamp, $status);
  343:     }
  344: 
  345: The extractor generates:
  346: 
  347:     ---
  348:     function: process_event
  349:     module: MyModule
  350:     input:
  351:       timestamp:
  352:         type: integer
  353:         # min: 0
  354:         # max: 2147483647
  355:         position: 0
  356:         _note: Unix timestamp
  357: 	semantic: unix_timestamp
  358:       status:
  359:         type: string
  360:         enum:
  361:           - active
  362:           - pending
  363:           - complete
  364:         position: 1
  365:         _note: 'Must be one of: active, pending, complete'
  366:       callback:
  367:         type: coderef
  368:         position: 2
  369:         _note: 'CODE reference - provide sub { } in tests'
  370: 
  371: =head1 RELATIONSHIP DETECTION
  372: 
  373: The schema extractor detects relationships and dependencies between parameters,
  374: enabling more sophisticated validation and test generation.
  375: 
  376: =head2 Relationship Types
  377: 
  378: =over 4
  379: 
  380: =item * B<mutually_exclusive>
  381: 
  382: Parameters that cannot be used together.
  383: 
  384:     die if $file && $content;  # Can't specify both
  385: 
  386: Generated schema:
  387: 
  388:     relationships:
  389:       - type: mutually_exclusive
  390:         params: [file, content]
  391:         description: Cannot specify both file and content
  392: 
  393: =item * B<required_group>
  394: 
  395: At least one parameter from the group must be specified (OR logic).
  396: 
  397:     die unless $id || $name;  # Must provide one
  398: 
  399: Generated schema:
  400: 
  401:     relationships:
  402:       - type: required_group
  403:         params: [id, name]
  404:         logic: or
  405:         description: Must specify either id or name
  406: 
  407: =item * B<conditional_requirement>
  408: 
  409: If one parameter is specified, another becomes required (IF-THEN logic).
  410: 
  411:     die if $async && !$callback;  # async requires callback
  412: 
  413: Generated schema:
  414: 
  415:     relationships:
  416:       - type: conditional_requirement
  417:         if: async
  418:         then_required: callback
  419:         description: When async is specified, callback is required
  420: 
  421: =item * B<dependency>
  422: 
  423: One parameter depends on another being present.
  424: 
  425:     die "Port requires host" if $port && !$host;
  426: 
  427: Generated schema:
  428: 
  429:     relationships:
  430:       - type: dependency
  431:         param: port
  432:         requires: host
  433:         description: port requires host to be specified
  434: 
  435: =item * B<value_constraint>
  436: 
  437: Specific value requirements between parameters.
  438: 
  439:     die if $ssl && $port != 443;  # ssl requires port 443
  440: 
  441: Generated schema:
  442: 
  443:     relationships:
  444:       - type: value_constraint
  445:         if: ssl
  446:         then: port
  447:         operator: ==
  448:         value: 443
  449:         description: When ssl is specified, port must equal 443
  450: 
  451: =item * B<value_conditional>
  452: 
  453: Parameter required when another has a specific value.
  454: 
  455:     die if $mode eq 'secure' && !$key;
  456: 
  457: Generated schema:
  458: 
  459:     relationships:
  460:       - type: value_conditional
  461:         if: mode
  462:         equals: secure
  463:         then_required: key
  464:         description: When mode equals 'secure', key is required
  465: 
  466: =back
  467: 
  468: =head2 Default Value Extraction
  469: 
  470: The extractor comprehensively extracts default values from both code and POD documentation:
  471: 
  472: =head3 Code Pattern Recognition
  473: 
  474: Extracts defaults from multiple Perl idioms:
  475: 
  476: =over 4
  477: 
  478: =item * Logical OR operator: C<$param = $param || 'default'>
  479: 
  480: =item * Defined-or operator: C<$param //= 'default'>
  481: 
  482: =item * Ternary operator: C<$param = defined $param ? $param : 'default'>
  483: 
  484: =item * Unless conditional: C<$param = 'default' unless defined $param>
  485: 
  486: =item * Chained defaults: C<$param = $param || $self->{_default} || 'fallback'>
  487: 
  488: =item * Multi-line patterns: C<$param = {} unless $param>
  489: 
  490: =back
  491: 
  492: =head3 POD Pattern Recognition
  493: 
  494: Extracts defaults from documentation:
  495: 
  496: =over 4
  497: 
  498: =item * Standard format: C<Default: 'value'>
  499: 
  500: =item * Alternative format: C<Defaults to: 'value'>
  501: 
  502: =item * Inline format: C<Optional, default: 'value'>
  503: 
  504: =item * Parameter lists: C<$param - type, default 'value'>
  505: 
  506: =back
  507: 
  508: =head3 Value Processing
  509: 
  510: Properly handles:
  511: 
  512: =over 4
  513: 
  514: =item * String literals with quotes and escape sequences
  515: 
  516: =item * Numeric values (integers and floats)
  517: 
  518: =item * Boolean values (true/false converted to 1/0)
  519: 
  520: =item * Empty data structures ([] and {})
  521: 
  522: =item * Special values (undef, __PACKAGE__)
  523: 
  524: =item * Complex expressions (preserved as-is when unevaluatable)
  525: 
  526: =item * Quote operators (q{}, qq{}, qw{})
  527: 
  528: =back
  529: 
  530: =head3 Type Inference
  531: 
  532: When a parameter has a default value but no explicit type annotation,
  533: the type is automatically inferred from the default:
  534: 
  535:     $options = {}        # inferred as hashref
  536:     $items = []          # inferred as arrayref
  537:     $count = 42          # inferred as integer
  538:     $ratio = 3.14        # inferred as number
  539:     $enabled = 1         # inferred as boolean
  540: 
  541: =head2 Context-Aware Return Analysis
  542: 
  543: The extractor provides comprehensive analysis of method return behavior,
  544: including context sensitivity, error handling conventions, and method chaining patterns.
  545: 
  546: =head3 List vs Scalar Context Detection
  547: 
  548: Automatically detects methods that return different values based on calling context:
  549: 
  550:     sub get_items {
  551:         my $self = $_[0];
  552:         return wantarray ? @items : scalar(@items);
  553:     }
  554: 
  555: Detection captures:
  556: 
  557: =over 4
  558: 
  559: =item * C<_context_aware> flag - Method uses wantarray
  560: 
  561: =item * C<_list_context> - Type returned in list context (e.g., 'array')
  562: 
  563: =item * C<_scalar_context> - Type returned in scalar context (e.g., 'integer')
  564: 
  565: =back
  566: 
  567: Recognizes both ternary operator patterns and conditional return patterns.
  568: 
  569: =head3 Void Context Methods
  570: 
  571: Identifies methods that don't return meaningful values:
  572: 
  573: =over 4
  574: 
  575: =item * Setters (C<set_*> methods)
  576: 
  577: =item * Mutators (C<add_*, remove_*, delete_*, clear_*, reset_*, update_*>)
  578: 
  579: =item * Loggers (C<log, debug, warn, error, info>)
  580: 
  581: =item * Methods with only empty returns
  582: 
  583: =back
  584: 
  585: Example:
  586: 
  587:     sub set_name {
  588:         my ($self, $name) = @_;
  589:         $self->{name} = $name;
  590:         return;  # Void context
  591:     }
  592: 
  593: Sets C<_void_context> flag and C<type =E<gt> 'void'>.
  594: 
  595: =head3 Method Chaining Detection
  596: 
  597: Identifies chainable methods that return C<$self> for fluent interfaces:
  598: 
  599:     sub set_width {
  600:         my ($self, $width) = @_;
  601:         $self->{width} = $width;
  602:         return $self;  # Chainable
  603:     }
  604: 
  605: Detection provides:
  606: 
  607: =over 4
  608: 
  609: =item * C<_returns_self> - Returns invocant for chaining
  610: 
  611: =item * C<class> - The class name being returned
  612: 
  613: =back
  614: 
  615: Also detects chaining documentation in POD (keywords: "chainable", "fluent interface",
  616: "returns self", "method chaining").
  617: 
  618: =head3 Error Return Conventions
  619: 
  620: Analyzes how methods signal errors:
  621: 
  622: B<Pattern Detection:>
  623: 
  624: =over 4
  625: 
  626: =item * C<undef_on_error> - Explicit C<return undef if/unless condition>
  627: 
  628: =item * C<implicit_undef> - Bare C<return if/unless condition>
  629: 
  630: =item * C<empty_list> - C<return ()> for list context errors
  631: 
  632: =item * C<zero_on_error> - Returns 0/false for boolean error indication
  633: 
  634: =item * C<exception_handling> - Uses eval blocks with error checking
  635: 
  636: =back
  637: 
  638: B<Example Analysis:>
  639: 
  640:     sub fetch_user {
  641:         my ($self, $id) = @_;
  642: 
  643:         return undef unless $id;        # undef_on_error
  644:         return undef if $id < 0;        # undef_on_error
  645: 
  646:         return $self->{users}{$id};
  647:     }
  648: 
  649: Results in:
  650: 
  651:     _error_return: 'undef'
  652:     _success_failure_pattern: 1
  653:     _error_handling: {
  654:         undef_on_error: ['$id', '$id < 0']
  655:     }
  656: 
  657: B<Success/Failure Pattern:>
  658: 
  659: Methods that return different types for success vs. failure are flagged with
  660: C<_success_failure_pattern>. Common patterns:
  661: 
  662: =over 4
  663: 
  664: =item * Returns value on success, undef on failure
  665: 
  666: =item * Returns true on success, false on failure
  667: 
  668: =item * Returns data on success, empty list on failure
  669: 
  670: =back
  671: 
  672: =head3 Success Indicator Detection
  673: 
  674: Methods that always return true (typically for side effects):
  675: 
  676:     sub update_status {
  677:         my ($self, $status) = @_;
  678:         $self->{status} = $status;
  679:         return 1;  # Success indicator
  680:     }
  681: 
  682: Sets C<_success_indicator> flag when method consistently returns 1.
  683: 
  684: =head3 Schema Output
  685: 
  686: Enhanced return analysis adds these fields to method schemas:
  687: 
  688:     output:
  689:       type: boolean              # Inferred return type
  690:       _context_aware: 1           # Uses wantarray
  691:       _list_context:
  692:         type: array
  693:       _scalar_context:
  694:         type: integer
  695:       _returns_self: 1               # Returns $self
  696:       _void_context: 1            # No meaningful return
  697:       _success_indicator: 1       # Always returns true
  698:       _error_return: undef        # How errors are signaled
  699:       _success_failure_pattern: 1 # Mixed return types
  700:       _error_handling:            # Detailed error patterns
  701:         undef_on_error: [...]
  702:         exception_handling: 1
  703: 
  704: This comprehensive analysis enables:
  705: 
  706: =over 4
  707: 
  708: =item * Better test generation (testing both contexts, error paths)
  709: 
  710: =item * Documentation generation (clear error conventions)
  711: 
  712: =item * API design validation (consistent error handling)
  713: 
  714: =item * Contract specification (precise return behavior)
  715: 
  716: =back
  717: 
  718: =head2 Example
  719: 
  720: For a method like:
  721: 
  722:     sub connect {
  723:         my ($self, $host, $port, $ssl, $file, $content) = @_;
  724: 
  725:         die if $file && $content;                    # mutually exclusive
  726:         die unless $host || $file;                   # required group
  727:         die "Port requires host" if $port && !$host; # dependency
  728:         die if $ssl && $port != 443;                 # value constraint
  729: 
  730:         # ... connection logic
  731:     }
  732: 
  733: The extractor generates:
  734: 
  735:     relationships:
  736:       - type: mutually_exclusive
  737:         params: [file, content]
  738:         description: Cannot specify both file and content
  739:       - type: required_group
  740:         params: [host, file]
  741:         logic: or
  742:         description: Must specify either host or file
  743:       - type: dependency
  744:         param: port
  745:         requires: host
  746:         description: port requires host to be specified
  747:       - type: value_constraint
  748:         if: ssl
  749:         then: port
  750:         operator: ==
  751:         value: 443
  752:         description: When ssl is specified, port must equal 443
  753: 
  754: =head1 MODERN PERL FEATURES
  755: 
  756: This module adds support for:
  757: 
  758: =head2 Subroutine Signatures (Perl 5.20+)
  759: 
  760:     sub connect($host, $port = 3306, %options) {
  761:         ...
  762:     }
  763: 
  764: Extracts: required params, optional params with defaults, slurpy params
  765: 
  766: =head2 Type Constraints (Perl 5.36+)
  767: 
  768:     sub calculate($x :Int, $y :Num) {
  769:         ...
  770:     }
  771: 
  772: Recognizes: Int, Num, Str, Bool, ArrayRef, HashRef, custom classes
  773: 
  774: =head3 Subroutine Attributes
  775: 
  776:     sub get_value :lvalue :Returns(Int) {
  777:         ...
  778:     }
  779: 
  780: Detects: :lvalue, :method, :Returns(Type), custom attributes
  781: 
  782: =head2 Postfix Dereferencing (Perl 5.20+)
  783: 
  784:     my @array = $arrayref->@*;
  785:     my %hash = $hashref->%*;
  786:     my @slice = $arrayref->@[1,3,5];
  787: 
  788: Tracks usage of modern dereferencing syntax
  789: 
  790: =head2 Field Declarations (Perl 5.38+)
  791: 
  792:     field $host :param = 'localhost';
  793:     field $port :param(port_number) = 3306;
  794:     field $logger :param :isa(Log::Any);
  795: 
  796: Extracts fields and maps them to parameters
  797: 
  798: =head2 Modern Perl Features Support
  799: 
  800: The schema extractor supports modern Perl syntax introduced in versions 5.20, 5.36, and 5.38+.
  801: 
  802: =head3 Subroutine Signatures (Perl 5.20+)
  803: 
  804: Automatically extracts parameters from native Perl signatures:
  805: 
  806:     use feature 'signatures';
  807: 
  808:     sub connect($host, $port = 3306, $database = undef) {
  809:         ...
  810:     }
  811: 
  812: Extracted schema includes:
  813: 
  814: =over 4
  815: 
  816: =item * Parameter positions
  817: 
  818: =item * Optional vs required parameters
  819: 
  820: =item * Default values from signature
  821: 
  822: =item * Slurpy parameters (@array, %hash)
  823: 
  824: =back
  825: 
  826: B<Example:>
  827: 
  828:     # Signature with defaults
  829:     sub process($file, %options) { ... }
  830: 
  831:     # Extracts:
  832:     # $file: position 0, required
  833:     # %options: position 1, optional, slurpy hash
  834: 
  835: =head3 Type Constraints in Signatures (Perl 5.36+)
  836: 
  837: Recognizes type constraints in signature parameters:
  838: 
  839:     sub calculate($x :Int, $y :Num, $name :Str = "result") {
  840:         return $x + $y;
  841:     }
  842: 
  843: Supported constraint types:
  844: 
  845: =over 4
  846: 
  847: =item * C<:Int, :Integer> -> integer
  848: 
  849: =item * C<:Num, :Number> -> number
  850: 
  851: =item * C<:Str, :String> -> string
  852: 
  853: =item * C<:Bool, :Boolean> -> boolean
  854: 
  855: =item * C<:ArrayRef, :Array> -> arrayref
  856: 
  857: =item * C<:HashRef, :Hash> -> hashref
  858: 
  859: =item * C<:ClassName> -> object with isa constraint
  860: 
  861: =back
  862: 
  863: Type constraints are combined with defaults when both are present.
  864: 
  865: =head3 Subroutine Attributes
  866: 
  867: Extracts and documents subroutine attributes:
  868: 
  869:     sub get_value :lvalue {
  870:         my $self = shift;
  871:         return $self->{value};
  872:     }
  873: 
  874:     sub calculate :Returns(Int) :method {
  875:         my ($self, $x, $y) = @_;
  876:         return $x + $y;
  877:     }
  878: 
  879: Recognized attributes stored in C<_attributes> field:
  880: 
  881: =over 4
  882: 
  883: =item * C<:lvalue> - Method can be assigned to
  884: 
  885: =item * C<:method> - Explicitly marked as method
  886: 
  887: =item * C<:Returns(Type)> - Declares return type
  888: 
  889: =item * Custom attributes with values: C<:MyAttr(value)>
  890: 
  891: =back
  892: 
  893: =head3 Postfix Dereferencing (Perl 5.20+)
  894: 
  895: Detects usage of postfix dereferencing syntax:
  896: 
  897:     use feature 'postderef';
  898: 
  899:     sub process_array {
  900:         my ($self, $arrayref) = @_;
  901:         my @array = $arrayref->@*;        # Array dereference
  902:         my @slice = $arrayref->@[1,3,5];  # Array slice
  903:         return @array;
  904:     }
  905: 
  906:     sub process_hash {
  907:         my ($self, $hashref) = @_;
  908:         my %hash = $hashref->%*;          # Hash dereference
  909:         return keys %hash;
  910:     }
  911: 
  912: Tracked features stored in C<_modern_features>:
  913: 
  914: =over 4
  915: 
  916: =item * C<array_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>@*>
  917: 
  918: =item * C<hash_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>%*>
  919: 
  920: =item * C<scalar_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>$*>
  921: 
  922: =item * C<code_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>&*>
  923: 
  924: =item * C<array_slice> - Uses C<-E<gt>@[...]>
  925: 
  926: =item * C<hash_slice> - Uses C<-E<gt>%{...}>
  927: 
  928: =back
  929: 
  930: =head3 Field Declarations (Perl 5.38+)
  931: 
  932: Extracts field declarations from class syntax and maps them to method parameters:
  933: 
  934:     use feature 'class';
  935: 
  936:     class DatabaseConnection {
  937:         field $host :param = 'localhost';
  938:         field $port :param = 3306;
  939:         field $username :param(user);
  940:         field $password :param;
  941:         field $logger :param :isa(Log::Any);
  942: 
  943:         method connect() {
  944:             # Fields available as instance variables
  945:         }
  946:     }
  947: 
  948: Field attributes:
  949: 
  950: =over 4
  951: 
  952: =item * C<:param> - Field is a constructor parameter (uses field name)
  953: 
  954: =item * C<:param(name)> - Field maps to parameter with different name
  955: 
  956: =item * C<:isa(Class)> - Type constraint for the field
  957: 
  958: =item * Default values in field declarations
  959: 
  960: =back
  961: 
  962: Extracted schema includes both field information in C<_fields> and merged parameter
  963: information in C<input>, allowing proper validation of class constructors.
  964: 
  965: =head3 Mixed Modern and Traditional Syntax
  966: 
  967: The extractor handles code that mixes modern and traditional syntax:
  968: 
  969:     sub modern($x, $y = 5) {
  970:         # Modern signature with default
  971:     }
  972: 
  973:     sub traditional {
  974:         my ($self, $x, $y) = @_;
  975:         $y //= 5;  # Traditional default in code
  976:         # Both extract same parameter information
  977:     }
  978: 
  979: Priority order for parameter information:
  980: 
  981: =over 4
  982: 
  983: =item 1. Signature declarations (highest priority)
  984: 
  985: =item 2. Field declarations (for class methods)
  986: 
  987: =item 3. POD documentation
  988: 
  989: =item 4. Code analysis (lowest priority)
  990: 
  991: =back
  992: 
  993: This ensures that explicit declarations in signatures take precedence over
  994: inferred information from code analysis.
  995: 
  996: =head3 Backwards Compatibility
  997: 
  998: All modern Perl feature detection is optional and automatic:
  999: 
 1000: =over 4
 1001: 
 1002: =item * Traditional C<sub> declarations continue to work
 1003: 
 1004: =item * Code without modern features extracts parameters as before
 1005: 
 1006: =item * Modern features are additive - they enhance rather than replace existing extraction
 1007: 
 1008: =item * Schemas include C<_source> field indicating where parameter info came from
 1009: 
 1010: =back
 1011: 
 1012: =head2 _yamltest_hints
 1013: 
 1014: Each method schema returned by L</extract_all> now optionally includes a
 1015: C<_yamltest_hints> key, which provides guidance for automated test generation
 1016: based on the code analysis.
 1017: 
 1018: This is intended to help L<App::Test::Generator> create meaningful tests,
 1019: including boundary and invalid input cases, without manually specifying them.
 1020: 
 1021: The structure is a hashref with the following keys:
 1022: 
 1023: =over 4
 1024: 
 1025: =item * boundary_values
 1026: 
 1027: An arrayref of numeric values that represent boundaries detected from
 1028: comparisons in the code. These are derived from literals in statements
 1029: like C<$x < 0> or C<$y >= 255>. The generator can use these to create
 1030: boundary tests.
 1031: 
 1032: Example:
 1033: 
 1034:     _yamltest_hints:
 1035:       boundary_values: [0, 1, 100, 255]
 1036: 
 1037: =item * invalid_inputs
 1038: 
 1039: An arrayref of values that are likely to be rejected by the method,
 1040: based on checks like C<defined>, empty strings, or numeric validations.
 1041: 
 1042: Example:
 1043: 
 1044:     _yamltest_hints:
 1045:       invalid_inputs: [undef, '', -1]
 1046: 
 1047: =item * equivalence_classes
 1048: 
 1049: An arrayref intended to capture detected equivalence classes or patterns
 1050: among inputs. Currently this is empty by default, but future enhancements
 1051: may populate it based on detected input groupings.
 1052: 
 1053: Example:
 1054: 
 1055:     _yamltest_hints:
 1056:       equivalence_classes: []
 1057: 
 1058: =back
 1059: 
 1060: =head3 Usage
 1061: 
 1062: When calling C<extract_all>, each method schema will include
 1063: C<_yamltest_hints> if any hints were detected:
 1064: 
 1065:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all;
 1066:     my $hints  = $schemas->{example_method}->{_yamltest_hints};
 1067: 
 1068: You can then feed these hints into automated test generators to produce
 1069: negative tests, boundary tests, and parameter-specific test cases.
 1070: 
 1071: =head3 Notes
 1072: 
 1073: =over 4
 1074: 
 1075: =item * Hints are inferred heuristically from code and validation statements.
 1076: 
 1077: =item * Not all inputs are guaranteed to be detected; the feature is additive
 1078: and will never remove information from the schema.
 1079: 
 1080: =item * Currently, equivalence classes are not populated, but the field exists
 1081: for future extension.
 1082: 
 1083: =item * Boundary and invalid input hints are deduplicated to avoid repeated
 1084: test values.
 1085: 
 1086: =back
 1087: 
 1088: =head3 Examples
 1089: 
 1090: Given a method like:
 1091: 
 1092:     sub example {
 1093:         my ($x) = @_;
 1094:         die "negative" if $x < 0;
 1095:         return unless defined($x);
 1096:         return $x * 2;
 1097:     }
 1098: 
 1099: After running:
 1100: 
 1101:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
 1102:         input_file => 'TestHints.pm',
 1103:         output_dir => '/tmp',
 1104:         quiet    => 1,
 1105:     );
 1106: 
 1107:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all;
 1108: 
 1109: The schema for the method "example" will include:
 1110: 
 1111:     $schemas->{example} = {
 1112:         function => 'example',
 1113:         _confidence => {
 1114:             input  => 'unknown',
 1115:             output => 'unknown',
 1116:         },
 1117:         input => {
 1118:             x => {
 1119:                 type     => 'scalar',
 1120:                 optional => 0,
 1121:             }
 1122:         },
 1123:         output => {
 1124:             type => 'scalar',
 1125:         },
 1126:         _yamltest_hints => {
 1127:             boundary_values => [0, 1],
 1128:             invalid_inputs  => [undef, -1],
 1129:             equivalence_classes => [],
 1130:         },
 1131:         _notes => '...',
 1132:         _analysis => {
 1133:             input_confidence  => 'low',
 1134:             output_confidence => 'unknown',
 1135:             confidence_factors => {
 1136:                 input  => {...},
 1137:                 output => {...},
 1138:             },
 1139:             overall_confidence => 'low',
 1140:         },
 1141:         _fields => {},
 1142:         _modern_features => {},
 1143:         _attributes => {},
 1144:     };
 1145: 
 1146: =head1 METHODS
 1147: 
 1148: =head2 new
 1149: 
 1150: Private methods are not included, unless C<include_private> is used in C<new()>.
 1151: 
 1152: The extractor supports several configuration parameters:
 1153: 
 1154:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
 1155:         input_file           => 'lib/MyModule.pm',  # Required
 1156:         output_dir           => 'schemas/',         # Optional - only needed if writing schemas
 1157:         verbose              => 1,                  # Default: 0
 1158:         include_private      => 1,                  # Default: 0
 1159:         max_parameters       => 50,                 # Default: 20
 1160:         confidence_threshold => 0.7,               # Default: 0.5
 1161:         strict_pod           => 0|1|2,              # Default: 0 (off)
 1162:     );
 1163: 
 1164: C<output_dir> is optional.
 1165: It is only required if schema files will be
 1166: written to disk. Callers that pass C<no_write =E<gt> 1> to C<extract_all>
 1167: do not need to supply it. If C<output_dir> is omitted and C<_write_schema>
 1168: is called, it will croak with a clear error message.
 1169: 
 1170: =cut
 1171:

 1199: 
 1200: =head2 extract_all
 1201: 
 1202: Extract schemas for all methods in the module.
 1203: 
 1204: Returns a hashref of method_name => schema.
 1205: 
 1206:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
 1207: 
 1208:     # Suppress writing .yml files to disk (returns schemas only)
 1209:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all(no_write => 1);
 1210: 
 1211: Accepts an optional hashref or named parameters:
 1212: 
 1213: =over 4
 1214: 
 1215: =item * C<no_write>
 1216: 
 1217: When set to a true value, schema files are not written to C<output_dir>.
 1218: The schemas hashref is still fully populated and returned.
 1219: This is useful when the caller wants to inspect or augment schemas
 1220: before deciding whether and where to write them.
 1221: 
 1222: =back
 1223: 
 1224: The extraction process performs comprehensive validation of the agreement between
 1225: POD documentation and the actual code, controlled by the C<strict_pod> option
 1226: specified in the constructor. This validation operates at three distinct levels:
 1227: 
 1228: =over 4
 1229: 
 1230: =item * C<0> (default, no validation)
 1231: 
 1232: No POD/code validation is performed. Any disagreements between the documented
 1233: parameters in POD and the actual parameters in the code are silently ignored.
 1234: The extractor proceeds with schema generation regardless of inconsistencies.
 1235: 
 1236: =item * C<1> (warning mode)
 1237: 
 1238: Validation errors are collected and attached to each method's schema under the
 1239: C<_pod_validation_errors> key. The extraction continues even when errors are found,
 1240: allowing batch processing and comprehensive reporting. Errors include:
 1241:   - Parameters documented in POD but not found in code signatures
 1242:   - Parameters present in code but undocumented in POD
 1243:   - Type mismatches (incompatible types flagged as "Type mismatch")
 1244:   - Type differences (compatible but different types flagged as "Type difference")
 1245:   - Optional/required status disagreements
 1246:   - Constraint mismatches (min/max bounds, regex patterns)
 1247: 
 1248: =item * C<2> (strict mode)
 1249: 
 1250: The extraction immediately C<croak>s when the first validation error is encountered,
 1251: providing a detailed error message. This mode is useful for enforcing documentation
 1252: quality in development pipelines or CI/CD processes. Even compatible type differences
 1253: (such as POD "integer" vs. code "number") will trigger failure in this mode.
 1254: 
 1255: =back
 1256: 
 1257: Validation checks encompass parameter existence, type compatibility, optional/required
 1258: status, and constraint consistency. The system distinguishes between "compatible"
 1259: type differences (e.g., "integer" and "number", "array" and "arrayref") which are
 1260: tolerated in warning mode but still reported, and "incompatible" type mismatches
 1261: (e.g., "string" vs. "hashref") which are always flagged as errors. A comprehensive
 1262: validation report can be generated using the C<generate_pod_validation_report> method.
 1263: 
 1264: =head3 Pseudo Code
 1265: 
 1266:   FOREACH method
 1267:   DO
 1268:     analyze the method
 1269:     write a schema file for that method (unless no_write is set)
 1270:   END
 1271: 
 1272: =cut
 1273:

 1330: 
 1331: =head2 _find_methods
 1332:

 2425: # --------------------------------------------------
 2426: # _extract_schema_hash_from_block
 2427: #

 2429: #             a PPI::Structure::Block node representing

 2438: # Side effects: None.
 2439: #
 2440: # Notes:      Delegates to _parse_schema_hash which
 2441: #             expects a PPI node with a children()

 2443: #             a clear semantic name at the call site.
 2444: # --------------------------------------------------

 5661: =head2 _analyze_relationships
 5662: 
 5663: Analyze relationships and dependencies between parameters.
 5664: 
 5665: Detects:
 5666: - Mutually exclusive parameters (can't use both)
 5667: - Required parameter groups (must use one of)
 5668: - Conditional requirements (if X then Y)
 5669: - Parameter dependencies (X requires Y)
 5670: - Value-based constraints (X=5 requires Y)
 5671: 
 5672: =cut
 5673:

 6414: =head2 _needs_object_instantiation
 6415: 
 6416: Enhanced object detection that:
 6417: - Detects factory methods that return instances
 6418: - Recognizes singleton patterns
 6419: - Identifies when constructor needs specific parameters
 6420: - Handles inheritance (when parent class new() is needed)
 6421: - Detects both instance methods and class methods that require objects
 6422: 
 6423: Returns:
 6424: - undef if no object needed
 6425: - package name if object instantiation is needed
 6426: - hashref with constructor details if specific parameters are needed
 6427: 
 6428: =cut
 6429:

 7068: =head2 _extract_default_value
 7069: 
 7070: Extract default values from common Perl patterns:
 7071: 
 7072: Patterns:
 7073:   - $param = $param || 'default_value'
 7074:   - $param //= 'default_value'
 7075:   - $param = defined $param ? $param : 'default'
 7076:   - $param = 'default' unless defined $param;
 7077:   - $param = $arg // 'default'
 7078:   - $param ||= 'default'
 7079: 
 7080: Returns the default value as a string if found, undef otherwise.
 7081: 
 7082: =cut

 7485: sub _validate_strictness_level {

 7487:

 7550: =head2 _log
 7551: 
 7552: Log a message if verbose mode is on.
 7553: 
 7554: =cut
 7555: 
 7556: sub _log {
 7557: 	my ($self, $msg) = @_;
 7558: 	print "$msg\n" if $self->{verbose};
 7559: }

 7561: =head1 NOTES
 7562: 
 7563: This is pre-pre-alpha proof of concept code.
 7564: Nevertheless,
 7565: it is useful for creating a template which you can modify to create a working schema to pass into L<App::Test::Generator>.
 7566:

 7568:

 7570: 
 7571: =item * L<App::Test::Generator> - Generate fuzz and corpus-driven test harnesses
 7572: 
 7573: Output from this module serves as input to that module.
 7574: So with well-documented code, you can automatically create your tests.
